# Fault Localization: ACPI Video Backlight Control Failure

- **Repository**: github.com/sg-evals/linux--55b2af1c (mirror of github.com/sg-evals)/linux--55b2af1c (mirror of torvalds/linux)
- **Kernel Version**: 5.6.7
- **Difficulty**: expert
- **Category**: fault_localization
- **Subsystem**: ACPI
- **Component**: Video/Backlight

## Bug Report

**Bug ID**: 207835
**Summary**: ACPI video backlight brightness control does not work on Acer TravelMate 5735Z by default

On the Intel GM45/GMA 4500MHD laptop with Debian Sid/unstable and Linux 5.6.7 and GNOME Shell 3.36.2, trying to change the brightness of the internal display using the function keys, GNOME shows the OSD, which seems to have five levels (from acer_wmi?), but the actual brightness does *not* change. There is only `/sys/class/backlight/intel_backlight/brightness` though, and writing values to it seems to work.

Booting the system with `acpi_backlight=vendor`, exposes `/sys/devices/platform/acer-wmi/backlight/acer-wmi/brightness`, but the behavior is the same.

Booting the system with `acpi_backlight=native` or `acpi_backlight=native`, changing the brightness with the function keys works, and there now seem to be 15 (or 16) levels.

```
$ grep '.*' /sys/class/dmi/id/*_* 2> /dev/null
/sys/class/dmi/id/bios_date:07/26/2011
/sys/class/dmi/id/bios_vendor:Acer
/sys/class/dmi/id/bios_version:V1.14
/sys/class/dmi/id/board_asset_tag:Base Board Asset Tag
/sys/class/dmi/id/board_name:BA51_MV
/sys/class/dmi/id/board_vendor:Acer
/sys/class/dmi/id/board_version:V1.14
/sys/class/dmi/id/chassis_asset_tag:
/sys/class/dmi/id/chassis_type:10
/sys/class/dmi/id/chassis_vendor:Acer
/sys/class/dmi/id/chassis_version:V1.14
/sys/class/dmi/id/product_family:Intel_Mobile
/sys/class/dmi/id/product_name:TravelMate 5735Z
/sys/class/dmi/id/product_sku:Montevina_Fab
/sys/class/dmi/id/product_version:V1.14
/sys/class/dmi/id/sys_vendor:Acer
```

## Task

1. Analyze the bug report to understand the symptoms and context

```json

  "confidence": 0.8,
  "reasoning": "Brief explanation of why these locations are the fault"
}
```

**Important**: Paths should be relative to the kernel source root (e.g., `kernel/sched/core.c`, not `/workspace/kernel/sched/core.c`).

48-assistanttext-
Perfect! My fault localization analysis is complete. Here's a summary of my findings:

## Fault Localization Summary

**Buggy File**: `drivers/acpi/video_detect.c`

**Buggy Element**: `video_detect_dmi_table` (static DMI quirks table)

**Confidence**: 95%

### Analysis

The Acer TravelMate 5735Z laptop has a backlight brightness control bug where:
- **Default behavior**: Brightness control doesn't work (GNOME shows OSD with 5 levels but actual brightness doesn't change)
- **With `acpi_backlight=native`**: Brightness control works perfectly (15-16 levels)

### Root Cause

The kernel's ACPI video backlight detection logic in `acpi_video_get_backlight_type()` doesn't have a DMI quirk entry for this specific hardware model. Without this entry, the kernel defaults to using the ACPI video backlight driver (which relies on acer-wmi on this system), which doesn't work properly on this hardware.

The system actually has a working native backlight interface (intel_backlight), but the default selection heuristic doesn't discover it because the ACPI video backlight interface is technically present in the BIOS.

### Fix Required

Add a new DMI entry to the `video_detect_dmi_table` in `drivers/acpi/video_detect.c` that matches the Acer TravelMate 5735Z and calls the `video_detect_force_native()` callback to force it to use the native backlight interface.

The result has been written to `/workspace/fault_localization_result.json`.

This table in drivers/acpi/video_detect.c is used to set device-specific backlight type preferences via acpi_video_get_backlight_type(). Without an entry for this model, the kernel defaults to using the ACPI video driver (acpi_backlight_video) instead of the native backlight interface (acpi_backlight_native) that actually works correctly. The bug report confirms that with acpi_backlight=native, the brightness control works perfectly with 15-16 levels, whereas the default behavior (which uses ACPI video / acer-wmi) shows 5 levels but doesn't actually change brightness. The fix requires adding a new DMI entry for the Acer TravelMate 5735Z (with matching sys_vendor='Acer', product_name='TravelMate 5735Z', and optionally board_name='BA51_MV') that calls video_detect_force_native() to force the kernel to use the native backlight interface for this specific hardware.\"\n}\n",

{
  "buggy_files": ["drivers/acpi/video_detect.c"],
  "buggy_functions": ["video_detect_dmi_table"],
  "confidence": 0.95,
  "reasoning": "The Acer TravelMate 5735Z is not present in the video_detect_dmi_table DMI quirks list. This table in drivers/acpi/video_detect.c is used to set device-specific backlight type preferences via acpi_video_get_backlight_type(). Without an entry for this model, the kernel defaults to using the ACPI video driver (acpi_backlight_video) instead of the native backlight interface (acpi_backlight_native) that actually works correctly. The bug report confirms that with acpi_backlight=native, the brightness control works perfectly with 15-16 levels, whereas the default behavior (which uses ACPI video / acer-wmi) shows 5 levels but doesn't actually change brightness. The fix requires adding a new DMI entry for the Acer TravelMate 5735Z (with matching sys_vendor='Acer', product_name='TravelMate 5735Z', and optionally board_name='BA51_MV') that calls video_detect_force_native() to force the kernel to use the native backlight interface for this specific hardware."
}
